#### $CANONICAL_PROJECT_DEFINITION_STATEMENT

**Preferred canonical name:** **$SPEECH_SCORE_ENGINE**.
**Canonical descriptive title:** **Speech-Score Composition System**.
**Permitted secondary designation:** **Post-Script Theatrical Composition Environment**.
This naming is the cleanest convergence of the project materials because it preserves the central claim that language is handled as semantic content, rhythmic material, and executable score, while also preserving the system-level scope across writing, notation, rehearsal, rendering, and live execution. [filecite: turn3file9turn3file17turn3file13]

#### 1. $DEFINITION

**$SPEECH_SCORE_ENGINE := a compositional system for authoring, analyzing, rehearsing, rendering, and performing polyvocal speech works in which text, timing, recurrence, vocal distribution, and spatial notation are interoperable across analog and digital forms.** Its core premise is that a dramatic utterance is never only text on a page; it is also a timed event, a vocal gesture, a positional relation among voices, and a repeatable performance object. [filecite: turn3file9turn3file12]

The system exists to convert language into a scored, repeatable, transformable performance object across page, audio, rehearsal, and live event. Its primary law is not merely that dialogue can be heard, but that meaning can be reorganized through timing, repetition, overlap, silence, redistribution, and recurrence without ceasing to be language. That is why the project is properly defined as a speech-score system rather than a script tool or voice utility. [filecite: turn3file13turn3file6turn3file17]

#### 2. $SYSTEM_SCOPE

Inside the canonical system boundary belong six domains: authorship, notation, analysis, rehearsal, rendering, and execution. Authorship covers the creation and transformation of phrase-events. Notation covers score-encoding of speech. Analysis covers dramaturgical and rhythmic inspection. Rehearsal covers the generation of performer-facing and conductor-facing artifacts. Rendering covers audio, score, and related output views. Execution covers live coordination of voices, cues, and timing states. This scope is explicit in the system materials and should remain stable. [filecite: turn3file12turn3file9]

The commercially accessible surface of the system may present as a **dramaturgical-audio workbench** or **listening-first revision environment for performative text**, but that is the entry layer, not the total ontology. The surface solves the immediate workflow problem of hearing and revising dialogue quickly. The deeper layer remains the polyphonic speech-composition engine. Internal documentation should preserve this two-layer distinction. [filecite: turn3file11turn3file14turn3file19]

#### 3. $STRICT_TERMINOLOGY

**$PHRASE_EVENT** is the primary compositional unit. Do not use “line” as the fundamental ontological term except when referring to imported legacy scripts. A line is a legacy textual presentation. A phrase-event is the actual system object: a bounded utterance or fragment with semantic content, speaker assignment, temporal position, duration behavior, and relational status. [filecite: turn3file12turn3file9]

**$VOICE_CHANNEL** is the canonical term for the speaking carrier in the system. Do not collapse this into “character” except in user-facing simplifications. A character may map to one or more voice-channels, and a voice-channel may carry character, chorus, synthetic, or abstract textual functions. The system therefore distinguishes character identity from voice-channel identity. [filecite: turn3file6turn3file17]

**$TEMPORAL_RELATION** is the primary organizing principle. Do not describe the system as plot-first, script-first, or scene-first at the deep-structure level. Scene remains a user-facing container, but temporal relation governs composition. This includes cue order, overlap, delay, subdivision, recurrence, silence, and relative entry logic. [filecite: turn3file17turn3file6]

**$TIMING_SUBSTRATE** is the canonical term for the temporal kernel. Do not replace it with vague terms like “playback settings” when discussing core architecture. The timing substrate handles clock time, beat time, relative cue time, and elastic time, and is what permits literary timing and compositional timing to coexist in one engine. [filecite: turn3file6]

**$NOTATION_RENDERER** is the canonical output term for score views. Do not refer to these outputs merely as “formatted scripts.” The renderer produces readable script view, rhythmic score view, spatial matrix view, and performer-specific part view. [filecite: turn3file6]

**$REHEARSAL_KERNEL** is the canonical bridge from composition objects to practical rehearsal artifacts. Use this instead of generic phrases like “practice mode” when referring to the system service. It generates cue sheets, click guides, count-ins, stems, and section isolations. [filecite: turn3file6]

**$LIVE_EXECUTION_LAYER** is the canonical term for real-time coordination during performance. Do not reduce this to “presentation mode.” It includes conductor view, countdown view, tempo map, monitor prompts, and rule-bound override behavior. [filecite: turn3file6]

**$ANALYSIS_ENGINE** is the canonical term for dramaturgical diagnostics. Do not call this “AI critique” in core documentation. Its job is narrower and more defensible: identification of pacing drag, weak speaker differentiation, rhythm monotony, broken interruption logic, overlong turns, and related structural issues. [filecite: turn3file6turn3file14]

#### 4. $EXCLUSIONS

The system is **not** canonically defined as text-to-speech software. Synthetic voice is infrastructure within the system, not the category to which the system belongs. Any naming, pitch, or documentation that frames the project primarily as a TTS layer weakens the ontology and collapses the moat. [filecite: turn3file9turn3file8turn3file19]

The system is **not** merely a playwriting app, a podcast maker, a voice generator, a screenplay reader, or a one-off experimental play framework. Those may be adjacent use cases, source materials, or entry surfaces, but the canonical project is the underlying generative framework for an entire class of works in which speech behaves as composed performance. [filecite: turn3file17turn3file13]

The system is **not** a total production-management platform. Costume, scenic design, payroll, ticketing, and unrelated production logistics remain outside the formal boundary unless later integrated as secondary modules. This exclusion should remain explicit in all architectural definitions. [filecite: turn3file12]

For MVP framing, the system is **not yet** defined by full overlap composition, conductor infrastructure, multimodal staging visualization, deep collaboration, or institutional administration. Those belong to later layers, not the canonical proof point. The first proof remains: users can hear and revise dialogue as performed time. [filecite: turn3file10turn3file15]

#### 5. $NAMING_RULES

At the **system level**, use **Title Case** for outward-facing category names and **$UPPER_SNAKE_CASE** for canonical internal entities. Example: “Speech-Score Composition System” in prose; **$SPEECH_SCORE_ENGINE** in specs. This keeps the conceptual name legible while preserving machine-like ontological precision.

At the **object level**, prefer names that indicate function rather than medium artifact. Use **$PHRASE_EVENT**, **$VOICE_CHANNEL**, **$TIMING_SUBSTRATE**, **$NOTATION_RENDERER**, **$REHEARSAL_KERNEL**, and **$LIVE_EXECUTION_LAYER**. Avoid weak nouns such as “block,” “piece,” “thing,” “snippet,” “clip,” or “dialogue chunk” in formal documentation unless they are explicitly mapped as aliases for onboarding.

At the **user-surface level**, permit simplified expressions only where adoption clarity requires them. “Scene,” “speaker,” “readback,” and “dialogue playback” are acceptable UX language, but internal schemas and specifications should always map those terms back to the deeper canonical object model. This preserves the long-term ontology while supporting the commercial wedge of a dramaturgical-audio studio. [filecite: turn3file11turn3file19]

At the **category level**, prefer names that preserve the project’s hybrid ontology. Approved pattern families are: **speech-score**, **polyvocal**, **post-script**, **dramaturgical-audio**, **performance-writing**, and **temporal writing intelligence**. Dispreferred pattern families are: **AI voice**, **script reader**, **podcast engine**, **theatre chatbot**, and **audio toy**, because they either over-trivialize or misclassify the system. [filecite: turn3file19turn3file14turn3file8]

At the **narrative level**, one sentence should always remain stable:

**The system treats language as a dual-aspect object: semantic content and timed performance.**

That sentence is the naming test. If a new label obscures either side of that duality, reject it. This follows directly from the system invariant that language must remain both meaning-bearing and temporally operative. [filecite: turn3file6]

#### 6. $CANONICAL_EXPRESSION_SET

Use this as the stable vocabulary core for future specs.

**Canonical master name:** Speech-Score Composition System.
**Canonical internal identifier:** $SPEECH_SCORE_ENGINE.
**Canonical product-surface descriptor:** Dramaturgical-Audio Workbench.
**Canonical deep-system descriptor:** Polyvocal Speech-Composition Engine.
**Canonical unit:** $PHRASE_EVENT.
**Canonical performer carrier:** $VOICE_CHANNEL.
**Canonical temporal kernel:** $TIMING_SUBSTRATE.
**Canonical score output service:** $NOTATION_RENDERER.
**Canonical rehearsal bridge:** $REHEARSAL_KERNEL.
**Canonical live layer:** $LIVE_EXECUTION_LAYER.
**Canonical diagnostic layer:** $ANALYSIS_ENGINE. [filecite: turn3file9turn3file6turn3file11]

#### 7. $FINAL_CANONICAL_STATEMENT

Here is the clean final form for reuse in future documents:

**$SPEECH_SCORE_ENGINE is a speech-score composition system for authoring, analyzing, rehearsing, rendering, and performing polyvocal works in which language functions simultaneously as meaning and as timed score. Its primary unit is the $PHRASE_EVENT; its primary organizing principle is temporal relation; its core purpose is to preserve translatability across page, audio, rehearsal, and live execution without collapsing the work into either inert prose or mere voice playback.** [filecite: turn3file9turn3file12turn3file6]

Next I can turn this into a **$TERMINOLOGY_CHARTER** with approved terms, forbidden terms, alias mappings, and repo-wide naming conventions.

### $TERMINOLOGY_CHARTER

#### $DOCUMENT_PURPOSE

This charter governs language across product copy, specifications, schema, API contracts, UI labels, repository structure, and implementation handoff. Its job is to prevent ontological drift. The system must remain legible as a speech-score composition system rather than collapsing into the weaker categories of script reader, voice utility, or generic TTS wrapper. [filecite: turn5file7] [filecite: turn5file19]

#### $GOVERNING_SENTENCE

**The system treats language as a dual-aspect object: semantic content and timed performance.**
Every naming decision must preserve both sides of that claim. If a term hides either meaning or temporal behavior, reject it. [filecite: turn5file7]

#### $CANONICAL_IDENTITY

| Layer | Canonical term | Status | Usage rule |
|---|---|---:|---|
| Master system name | Speech-Score Composition System | Approved | Use in external prose, formal category language, deck copy, and high-level documentation |
| Internal system identifier | `$SPEECH_SCORE_ENGINE` | Approved | Use in specifications, architecture docs, schemas, and repo-level ontology |
| Product-surface descriptor | Dramaturgical-Audio Workbench | Approved | Use for adoptable commercial surface and user-facing product explanation |
| Deep-system descriptor | Polyvocal Speech-Composition Engine | Approved | Use when distinguishing deeper compositional layer from the initial product wedge |
| Secondary designation | Post-Script Theatrical Composition Environment | Permitted | Use selectively in theoretical or manifesto-style contexts |
| Category shorthand | Speech-score system | Approved | Use when compactness is needed without loss of ontology |

These expressions are the stable vocabulary core and should remain fixed unless the ontology itself changes. [filecite: turn5file7] [filecite: turn5file9]

#### $APPROVED_TERMS

| Canonical term | Definition | Preferred scope |
|---|---|---|
| `$PHRASE_EVENT` | Primary compositional unit; a bounded utterance or fragment with semantic, temporal, and relational properties | Data model, theory, architecture, score logic |
| `$VOICE_CHANNEL` | Speaking carrier independent from literary character identity | Data model, rendering, analysis, live execution |
| `$TEMPORAL_RELATION` | Primary organizing principle governing cue order, overlap, delay, recurrence, silence, and entry logic | Theory, architecture, diagnostics |
| `$TIMING_SUBSTRATE` | Temporal kernel supporting clock, beat, cue-relative, and elastic time | Architecture, implementation, timing services |
| `$NOTATION_RENDERER` | Service producing readable script, rhythmic score, spatial matrix, and performer part views | Output layer, rendering subsystem |
| `$REHEARSAL_KERNEL` | Bridge translating composition objects into cue sheets, drills, stems, and count structures | Rehearsal tooling, exports |
| `$LIVE_EXECUTION_LAYER` | Real-time coordination layer for performance control and override | Performance infrastructure |
| `$ANALYSIS_ENGINE` | Dramaturgical diagnostic layer for timing, pacing, speaker differentiation, repetition, and interruption logic | Product diagnostics, analysis subsystem |
| `$COMPOSITION_LAYER` | Authoring environment for phrase-events, recurrence rules, and structural transformations | Product architecture |
| `$PHRASE_EVENT_MODEL` | Canonical structured representation of utterance-level objects | Data modeling, persistence |
| `$READABLE_SCRIPT` | Literary-readable output view | Output naming |
| `$RHYTHMIC_SCORE` | Beat- or measure-oriented output view | Output naming |
| `$SPATIAL_TEXT_SCORE` | Layout-driven score view where typography carries instruction | Output naming |
| `$TABLE_READ_AUDIO` | Rapid auditory draft for dramaturgical listening | Product surface, MVP |
| `$REHEARSAL_PACK` | Export bundle for performers and directors | Output naming |
| `$CONDUCTOR_VIEW` | Control-oriented live view for timing and branching | Later-stage execution layer |
| `$LIVE_PROMPT_VIEW` | Monitor-safe live text display | Later-stage execution layer |
| `$MACHINE_SCORE_OBJECT` | Structured machine-readable score artifact | Export, API, storage |
| `$KINETIC_TEXT_RENDER` | Projection or motion-based visual text output | Advanced output layer |

These terms follow directly from the current conceptual system and output model. [filecite: turn5file5] [filecite: turn5file6] [filecite: turn5file8]

#### $FORBIDDEN_TERMS

| Forbidden term | Why it is rejected | Replacement |
|---|---|---|
| text-to-speech software | Reduces the system to commodity voice infrastructure | Speech-Score Composition System |
| TTS tool | Flattens ontology and moat | Dramaturgical-Audio Workbench |
| voice generator | Centers the wrong substrate | Table-read audio renderer, voice layer, or render service |
| script reader | Treats the work as inert text | Listening-first revision environment for performative text |
| podcast engine | Misclassifies the medium and excludes live/rehearsal/score dimensions | Speech-score system |
| playwriting app | Too narrow and literature-bound | Dramaturgical-Audio Workbench |
| screenplay reader | Misframes the use case and omits compositional depth | Dialogue revision environment |
| theatre chatbot | Category error | Analysis engine or dramaturgical diagnostic layer |
| audio toy | Trivializing language that weakens institutional seriousness | Product or system term appropriate to layer |
| playback settings | Too vague for the temporal kernel | `$TIMING_SUBSTRATE` |
| formatted script | Too weak for the output model | `$NOTATION_RENDERER` output |
| practice mode | Understates formal rehearsal function | `$REHEARSAL_KERNEL` |
| presentation mode | Understates real-time coordination and override | `$LIVE_EXECUTION_LAYER` |
| AI critique | Overclaims and weakens diagnostic seriousness | `$ANALYSIS_ENGINE` |
| dialogue chunk | Loose and under-specified | `$PHRASE_EVENT` |
| clip | Imports DAW/video baggage and obscures semantic status | `$PHRASE_EVENT` |
| thing / piece / block / snippet | Ontologically weak | Use the precise canonical object term |

These exclusions are not stylistic niceties; they protect the system from being reclassified into commodity categories. [filecite: turn5file19] [filecite: turn5file17] [filecite: turn5file18]

#### $ALIAS_MAPPINGS

| User-surface term | Internal canonical term | Rule |
|---|---|---|
| scene | `$SCENE` as container, but conceptually subordinate to `$PHRASE_EVENT` and `$TEMPORAL_RELATION` | Allowed in UI; do not treat as deepest unit in specs |
| speaker | `$VOICE_CHANNEL` | Allowed in UI and onboarding; map back internally |
| character | `$VOICE_CHANNEL` or character-to-channel mapping | Allowed only when referring to literary source identity |
| line | `$PHRASE_EVENT` | Allowed for imported scripts and simple editing views; avoid in core ontology |
| readback | `$TABLE_READ_AUDIO` or render playback | Allowed in product copy; avoid in architectural docs |
| dialogue playback | `$TABLE_READ_AUDIO` on the surface, `$TIMING_SUBSTRATE` + render flow underneath | Allowed in product copy |
| script view | `$READABLE_SCRIPT` | Prefer canonical output name in docs |
| score view | `$RHYTHMIC_SCORE` or `$SPATIAL_TEXT_SCORE` | Use precise output name when known |
| voice | voice profile or `$VOICE_CHANNEL`, depending context | Distinguish synthetic voice profile from compositional carrier |
| rehearsal export | `$REHEARSAL_PACK` | Prefer canonical form in docs |
| live mode | `$LIVE_EXECUTION_LAYER` | UI shorthand only |
| diagnostics | `$ANALYSIS_ENGINE` output | Use “diagnostics” in UI; use engine name in architecture |

This preserves adoption-friendly language at the interface while keeping the deeper ontology intact in code and specification. [filecite: turn5file16] [filecite: turn5file18]

#### $APPROVED_PATTERN_FAMILIES

| Pattern family | Status | Notes |
|---|---:|---|
| speech-score | Approved | Best high-level hybrid descriptor |
| polyvocal | Approved | Best descriptor for distributed voice architecture |
| post-script | Approved | Strong theoretical framing |
| dramaturgical-audio | Approved | Best product-surface framing |
| performance-writing | Approved | Good bridge term for general audiences |
| temporal writing intelligence | Approved | Strong positioning term for moat language |

#### $DISPREFERRED_PATTERN_FAMILIES

| Pattern family | Status | Notes |
|---|---:|---|
| AI voice | Rejected | Centers commodity infrastructure |
| script reader | Rejected | Literature-bound reduction |
| podcast engine | Rejected | Category narrowing |
| theatre chatbot | Rejected | Nonsensical framing |
| audio toy | Rejected | Trivializing and unserious |

These pattern families were already implicit in the prior naming rules and product-surface strategy. [filecite: turn5file16] [filecite: turn5file18]

#### $REPO_WIDE_NAMING_CONVENTIONS

##### $CONVENTION_01_SYSTEM_AND_ONTOLOGY_NAMES

External category names use **Title Case**. Internal ontological entities use **`$UPPER_SNAKE_CASE`**. This rule is already established and should be universal across specifications, ADRs, architecture notes, and formal schemas. [filecite: turn5file16]

Examples:

```text
Speech-Score Composition System
Dramaturgical-Audio Workbench
Polyvocal Speech-Composition Engine

$SPEECH_SCORE_ENGINE
$PHRASE_EVENT
$VOICE_CHANNEL
$TIMING_SUBSTRATE
$ANALYSIS_ENGINE
```

##### $CONVENTION_02_DATABASE_IDENTIFIERS

Database tables, columns, and SQL artifacts use **lowercase snake_case** without `$` prefixes. This follows the existing repository blueprint and migration stubs. [filecite: turn5file13]

Examples:

```sql
app_user
scene
scene_version
version_line
playback_render
diagnostic_report
share_link
created_at
estimated_duration_ms
```

##### $CONVENTION_03_TYPESCRIPT_EXPORTED_TYPES

Exported interfaces, types, classes, React components, and service contracts use **PascalCase**. Internal field names use **camelCase**. This follows the implementation handoff package and interface contracts. [filecite: turn5file15]

Examples:

```ts
ParseSceneResult
CreateSceneVersionInput
RenderDispatchService
VoiceProviderAdapter

sceneId
versionId
renderScope
estimatedDurationMs
```

##### $CONVENTION_04_FILE_AND_DIRECTORY_NAMES

Files and directories use **kebab-case** for human-legible artifact names and workflow modules, except where framework conventions require otherwise. Domain module directories should reflect ontology, not generic utilities. This follows the repo blueprint’s modular structure. [filecite: turn5file13]

Examples:

```text
docs/architecture/002-domain-model.md
apps/api/src/services/render-dispatch.service.ts
packages/domain/src/parsing/parse-scene-input.ts
packages/database/migrations/0003_add_scene_versions_version_lines.sql
```

##### $CONVENTION_05_API_PATHS

HTTP routes use **lowercase plural resource nouns** and stable version prefixes. Do not place theoretical vocabulary directly into public API paths unless the concept is truly public-facing. API surface should remain operationally legible. [filecite: turn5file15]

Examples:

```text
/api/v1/projects
/api/v1/scenes/{scene_id}
/api/v1/versions/{version_id}/renders
/api/v1/versions/{version_id}/diagnostics/latest
```

##### $CONVENTION_06_EVENT_NAMES

Domain events use **noun.action.state** in lowercase dot notation. This convention is already proposed for render, parse, playback, version, and share flows and should be enforced universally. [filecite: turn5file13]

Examples:

```text
scene.parse.requested
scene.parse.committed
version.created
render.completed
playback.started
diagnostic.viewed
share.revoked
```

##### $CONVENTION_07_ENVIRONMENT_VARIABLES

Environment variables remain **`$UPPER_SNAKE_CASE`** and environment-first configuration remains mandatory. This is already aligned with the implementation package. [filecite: turn5file15]

Examples:

```bash
$DATABASE_URL
$REDIS_URL
$VOICE_PROVIDER_API_KEY
$APP_BASE_URL
$PUBLIC_SHARE_BASE_URL
$LOG_LEVEL
```

##### $CONVENTION_08_DOC_ARTIFACT_IDS

Formal documents should continue using stable IDs in the form:

```text
<domain-subject>_<artifact-class>_<YYYYMMDD>
```

Examples:

```text
audio-dramaturgical-studio_mvp-system-design-package_20260327
audio-dramaturgical-studio_repository-blueprint-and-handoff_20260327
```

This matches the current document style and preserves machine-sortable continuity. [filecite: turn5file13]

#### $SEMANTIC_BOUNDARY_RULES

The system must always be named from the inside out.

When referring to the ontology, use composition language.
When referring to the product wedge, use listening-and-revision language.
When referring to infrastructure, use render, provider, storage, queue, and contract language.
Do not let infrastructure names overwrite ontology names.

That means the following distinction must remain permanent:

The system is a **speech-score composition system**.
The product surface is a **dramaturgical-audio workbench**.
The voice layer is only infrastructure. [filecite: turn5file7] [filecite: turn5file9] [filecite: turn5file18]

#### $NAMING_TESTS

A proposed term is acceptable only if it passes all four tests.

| Test | Question | Pass condition |
|---|---|---|
| Dual-aspect test | Does the term preserve both meaning and timed performance? | Must preserve both |
| Depth test | Does the term fit the deeper system, not only the MVP surface? | Must scale upward |
| Non-commodification test | Does the term avoid collapsing the product into commodity voice tooling? | Must avoid TTS-first framing |
| Translation test | Does the term remain valid across page, audio, rehearsal, and live execution? | Must remain cross-medium valid |

These tests follow directly from the project’s canonical definition and invariants. [filecite: turn5file6] [filecite: turn5file7]

#### $ENFORCEMENT_RULE

In cases of conflict, the order of authority is:

| Priority | Source of truth |
|---|---|
| 1 | `$GOVERNING_SENTENCE` |
| 2 | `$CANONICAL_IDENTITY` |
| 3 | `$APPROVED_TERMS` |
| 4 | `$ALIAS_MAPPINGS` |
| 5 | product-surface simplifications |

If a UI term conflicts with ontology, the UI term stays local to UI only. It must not leak into schema, API contracts, or architectural language.

#### $FINAL_CHARTER_STATEMENT

**All repository, product, and documentation language must preserve the system’s identity as a speech-score composition system whose fundamental object is not inert text but structured temporal language. Use adoption-friendly aliases at the surface where useful, but preserve canonical internal terms in schema, contracts, architecture, and code. Do not name the system as a TTS tool, script reader, or voice generator.** [filecite: turn5file19] [filecite: turn5file9]

The next clean artifact is a **`$LEXICON_AND_STYLE_GUIDE.md`** file formatted exactly as a repo document, ready to drop into `docs/architecture/`.

# dramaturgist-tuning - 05 Tracker and Ableton Features

## dramaturgist-tuning - 05 Tracker and Ableton Features -- 001 Prompt / Response

File: [dramaturgist-tuning-05--tracker-and-ableton-features--001-prompt-response.md](dramaturgist-tuning-05--tracker-and-ableton-features--001-prompt-response.md)  
Pair ID: `dt-05-001`  
Content SHA-256: `5cc4a9ed3027dd0ad7cee838007f7bfde91846b01bb96d531fe6467863940145`

## Prompt

Message ID: `ec2783f4-5b34-4222-afa8-24fd13ebae46`
Created UTC: `2026-03-28T04:08:44.427000Z`

i want this product to have tracker & ableton features

## Response

##### Response Segment 1

Message ID: `77a1c1e7-d66c-4be5-9276-3348aa65325a`
Created UTC: `2026-03-28T04:08:45.799403Z`
Model: `gpt-5-4-thinking`

I’m grounding this in the actual tracker and Ableton interaction models, then I’ll fold them into your speech-score product as a concrete hybrid feature set.

##### Response Segment 2

Message ID: `d4274a9c-3477-4975-aaea-d99b4f1b517e`
Created UTC: `2026-03-28T04:09:13.387677Z`
Model: `gpt-5-4-thinking`

Yes. That is the right move.

The product should be **tracker-brained and Ableton-bodied**.

Your existing concept already points toward a speech-score system where language is treated as timed performance rather than inert text. The missing step is to formalize the interaction model around two proven musical paradigms: the tracker’s **row-precise event grid** and Live’s **clip-launch / arrangement duality**. [filecite: turn0file4] [filecite: turn0file12turn0file13]

#### What each side contributes

| Source model | What it does well | What your product should inherit |
|---|---|---|
| Tracker | Notes/events entered top-to-bottom in patterns; patterns sequenced into larger form; per-step effect commands and phrase logic are core, not secondary [cite: turn968472view3turn968472view4turn968472view5] | Phrase-event grid, row-level speech commands, exact timing, repeat logic, micro-edits, deterministic execution |
| Ableton Session View | Clips can be played in any order; the grid is random-access and launch-oriented rather than fixed-sequence [cite: turn968472view0turn968472view1] | Scene / phrase launching, live audition, improvisatory recombination, rehearsal triggering |
| Ableton Arrangement View | Linear timeline with locators, automation lanes, section launching, clip movement, time-signature changes [cite: turn706544view0turn706544view2] | Long-form structure, revision timeline, section markers, tempo maps, arrangement of speech events across full works |
| Ableton Clip/Warp model | Clips have editable playback properties; warping keeps audio aligned to tempo and lets markers lock points to timeline positions [cite: turn968472view2turn351283search6] | Spoken-phrase anchors, breath/transient alignment, elastic retiming of speech without destroying phrase identity |
| Ableton Racks / Macros | Multiple parameters can be grouped behind macro controls; racks can nest and encapsulate complex behavior [cite: turn706544view1] | Voice-chain presets, dramaturgical macro controls, reusable phrase-performance modules |

#### The synthesis

Do **not** make it “a DAW for theatre” in the generic sense.

Make it a **speech-score workstation** with two primary views:

##### 1. Pattern View
This is the tracker layer.

Rows are discrete time units. Columns are voice-channels. Cells contain phrase-events plus command data. Renoise’s pattern editor is explicitly built around entering events from top to bottom, arranging multiple tracks inside a pattern, and sequencing patterns into larger form; effect commands are central because they can control volume, automation, playback, and direct sample manipulation at exact positions. [cite: turn968472view3turn968472view4]

In your product, a cell should not just hold text. It should hold:

`$PHRASE_EVENT`
`$VOICE_CHANNEL`
`$START_ROW`
`$DURATION_RULE`
`$REPEAT_RULE`
`$INTENSITY`
`$PAN / STAGE_POSITION`
`$OVERLAP_FLAG`
`$COMMANDS`

This is where the tracker inheritance matters most.

##### 2. Launch / Arrangement View
This is the Ableton layer.

One surface should work like Session View: phrase-clips and scene-clips launch in any order, for rehearsal, exploration, table-read auditioning, and live recombination. Live’s Session grid is explicitly random-access; clip launch behavior can be trigger, gate, toggle, or repeat. [cite: turn968472view0turn968472view1]

The other surface should work like Arrangement View: the full work unfolds on a linear timeline with locators, launchable sections, automation lanes, and section-level structural control. Live’s Arrangement supports locators, automation lanes, and timeline-based playback control in bars/beats and clock time. [cite: turn706544view0turn706544view2]

That duality is exactly right for you because your product needs both:

the **compositional precision** of a score editor, and
the **live plasticity** of a rehearsal / performance engine. [filecite: turn0file4]

#### The actual feature set you should add

##### Tracker-derived features

| Feature | Why it belongs |
|---|---|
| Row-based phrase editor | Lets speech be entered as discrete timed events instead of prose blocks |
| Per-cell command columns | This is the decisive tracker inheritance; each phrase-event can carry exact behavior |
| Pattern sequencing | Lets sections recur, mutate, and recombine efficiently |
| Phrase sub-editors | Renoise phrases are triggered by notes and can act as reusable embedded structures [cite: turn968472view5] |
| Deterministic playback | Essential for rehearsal trust and score repeatability |
| Fast keyboard-first entry | Required if the tool is to feel compositional rather than word-processor-like |
| Interpolation / batch edit tools | Trackers excel at structural editing of many events at once; your speech system needs the equivalent |

##### Ableton-derived features

| Feature | Why it belongs |
|---|---|
| Clip-based scene launching | Lets users audition variants instantly |
| Session grid | Best interface for trying alternate readings and combinations |
| Arrangement timeline | Needed for full work construction |
| Warp anchors for spoken audio | Lets recorded or synthetic speech align to tempo / structure without losing semantic identity [cite: turn968472view2] |
| Automation lanes | Needed for density, intensity, panning, effects, spatialization, emphasis, timing drift [cite: turn706544view2] |
| Locators / section markers | Crucial for rehearsal navigation and repeatable entry points [cite: turn706544view0] |
| Racks / macros | Best abstraction for packaging performance behaviors into reusable controls [cite: turn706544view1] |

#### What the speech-specific equivalents should be

This is where the hybrid becomes yours rather than imitation.

| Music-software concept | Speech-score equivalent |
|---|---|
| Note | `$PHRASE_EVENT` |
| Track | `$VOICE_CHANNEL` |
| Pattern | `$PASSAGE_PATTERN` |
| Song order / arrangement | `$WORK_TIMELINE` |
| Clip | `$PHRASE_CLIP` or `$SCENE_CLIP` |
| Effect command | `$SPEECH_COMMAND` |
| Warp marker | `$UTTERANCE_ANCHOR` |
| Macro | `$DRAMATURGICAL_MACRO` |
| Rack | `$VOICE_BEHAVIOR_RACK` |
| Automation lane | `$PERFORMANCE_ENVELOPE` |

#### The speech commands you should support

This is the strongest tracker import. Renoise’s effect-command logic is exactly the right precedent because it treats local event instructions as first-class. [cite: turn968472view4]

Your command set should eventually include something like this:

| Command | Function |
|---|---|
| `PA` | pause after event |
| `PR` | pre-roll delay before speech |
| `RP` | repeat count |
| `RT` | ratchet / retrigger subdivision |
| `OV` | overlap enable |
| `CU` | cue another voice-channel |
| `EM` | emphasis amount |
| `DN` | density multiplier |
| `PN` | pan / spatial position |
| `BR` | breath insertion |
| `ST` | stutter |
| `GL` | glide tempo / pacing between events |
| `MX` | macro trigger |
| `LK` | lock to anchor |
| `HU` | humanization range |
| `MT` | mute or ghost utterance |
| `TR` | transform text delivery mode |

This is the exact point where your system stops being “dialogue playback” and becomes compositional infrastructure.

#### The three views I would make canonical

##### `$PATTERN_VIEW`
Tracker-native. Keyboard-first. Dense. Exact. Best for writing and micro-editing.

##### `$SESSION_VIEW`
Ableton-native. Launch grid for phrases, passages, and scenes. Best for audition, rehearsal, and modular recombination.

##### `$ARRANGEMENT_VIEW`
Timeline-native. Best for final form, pacing arcs, automation, locators, and export.

That triad would give the system a real internal logic.

#### What should be in MVP and what should wait

##### MVP
Keep the hybrid visible, but not total.

The MVP should include:

a basic Session-style launch grid,
a basic Arrangement-style timeline,
a simplified Pattern view for phrase rows,
voice-channels,
clip / scene triggering,
global tempo plus per-event pause values,
basic performance envelopes,
versioned table-read audio,
locator markers,
and at least a first pass at per-cell speech commands.

That is already a strong wedge. It still aligns with the narrower product thesis from the earlier docs: hear dialogue quickly, inspect timing, revise against sound. [filecite: turn0file7turn0file8]

##### Later
Defer the heavier tracker layer until the workflow proves itself.

Later phases should add:

true overlap polyphony,
nested phrases,
macro-rack systems,
advanced command language,
live conductor view,
external control-surface support,
elastic spoken-audio warping,
and score export that fully reflects pattern logic.

#### The design principle

The cleanest principle is this:

**Ableton governs macro-form and performance navigation.
Tracker logic governs micro-form and event control.**

That division is stable and coherent.

Ableton gives you:
launching, arrangement, automation, locators, macros, live feel. [cite: turn968472view0turn706544view0turn706544view1turn706544view2]

Tracker design gives you:
precision, command density, repeatable event logic, phrase-level recursion, and exact control over local behavior. [cite: turn968472view3turn968472view4turn968472view5]

#### The sentence I would use internally

**Build the Speech-Score Composition System as a hybrid of tracker precision and Ableton-style launch/arrangement control.** The tracker layer should define how phrase-events are encoded; the Ableton layer should define how phrase-events are organized, triggered, automated, and performed. This remains fully consistent with the current project ontology. [filecite: turn0file12turn0file13]

#### Bottom line

You are right.

This product should not choose between tracker and Ableton paradigms. It should fuse them.

The best version is:

**tracker event grammar + Ableton clip ecology + your speech-score ontology.**

That gives you a real moat.

If you want, the next logical step is for me to turn this into a revised product spec with a concrete screen model for `$PATTERN_VIEW`, `$SESSION_VIEW`, and `$ARRANGEMENT_VIEW`.


## dramaturgist-tuning - 05 Tracker and Ableton Features -- 002 Prompt / Response

Pair ID: `dt-05-002`  
Content SHA-256: `37e1f67b81bd0ca1ddc31423253847cc99026a4461b95678ec3a9b82e80ae36c`

## Prompt

Message ID: `2c103a4f-14d1-45a2-b43d-f1087713af87`
Created UTC: `2026-03-28T04:10:59.379000Z`

the next logical step is for me to turn this into a revised product spec with a concrete screen model for $PATTERN_VIEW, $SESSION_VIEW, and $ARRANGEMENT_VIEW.

## Response

##### Response Segment 1

Message ID: `cb4de587-23c8-4088-8632-c31f63246afd`

##### Response Segment 2

Message ID: `1d6be921-3595-4d97-a90f-94ade135603b`
Created UTC: `2026-03-28T04:11:01.797622Z`
Model: `gpt-5-4-thinking`

Agreed. Here is the revised product spec, centered on three concrete work surfaces and kept inside the existing ontology of the **Speech-Score Composition System** rather than drifting into generic DAW language. The governing rule remains unchanged: language is a dual-aspect object, carrying both semantic content and timed performance. The product surface may remain a dramaturgical-audio workbench, but the internal system is still a polyvocal speech-composition engine. [filecite: turn1file63] [filecite: turn1file64] [filecite: turn1file65]

### Revised Product Specification
#### `$SPEECH_SCORE_ENGINE`
#### Screen Model for `$PATTERN_VIEW`, `$SESSION_VIEW`, and `$ARRANGEMENT_VIEW`

##### 1. Product frame

The product has one commercial entry promise and one deeper structural promise.

The commercial promise is: **hear, inspect, and revise dialogue as performed time before rehearsal**. The structural promise is: **compose speech as score across writing, notation, rehearsal, rendering, and execution**. That two-layer distinction should remain explicit in the revised spec. [filecite: turn1file58] [filecite: turn1file59]

The revised interface therefore needs three distinct but interoperable work surfaces:

| View | Primary function | Temporal scale | Primary user mode |
|---|---|---|---|
| `$PATTERN_VIEW` | micro-composition and event control | row / beat / phrase-event | writing as score |
| `$SESSION_VIEW` | launch, audition, recombination, rehearsal exploration | passage / section | exploratory performance |
| `$ARRANGEMENT_VIEW` | full-work structure, pacing arcs, automation, export | movement / work timeline | formal composition and finalization |

This triad follows directly from the tracker-precision plus Ableton-style launch/arrangement model, but the system’s canonical objects remain `$PHRASE_EVENT`, `$VOICE_CHANNEL`, `$TEMPORAL_RELATION`, and `$TIMING_SUBSTRATE`. The DAW analogy is descriptive, not ontological. [filecite: turn1file67] [filecite: turn1file63]

---

##### 2. Shared system rules across all three views

Every view operates on the same underlying composition object. The views are not separate editors with lossy translation between them. They are different renderings of one machine-readable score state. That preserves the core invariant that page, audio, and performance must remain translatable without rewriting the work. [filecite: turn1file57]

The shared object model for the revised product spec is:

| Canonical object | Role in UI |
|---|---|
| `$WORK` | top-level projectable composition |
| `$MOVEMENT` | large formal section on the work timeline |
| `$PASSAGE` | grouped set of phrase-events |
| `$PHRASE_EVENT` | smallest timed semantic unit |
| `$VOICE_CHANNEL` | speaking carrier |
| `$PERFORMANCE_ENVELOPE` | automation or modulation over time |
| `$UTTERANCE_ANCHOR` | fixed alignment point for spoken audio or render timing |
| `$REHEARSAL_PACK` | performer-facing output |
| `$TABLE_READ_AUDIO` | rapid auditory draft |

User-surface aliases such as “scene,” “speaker,” and “line” may still appear in the product where usability requires it, but the architecture and implementation should continue to map them internally to the canonical terms above. [filecite: turn1file64] [filecite: turn1file65]

---

##### 3. Global application shell

All three views should sit inside one stable shell so that mode-switching does not feel like entering a different product.

| Region | Function |
|---|---|
| Top command bar | project title, save state, render state, transport, tempo, meter, current version |
| Left structure rail | work tree: project → work → movement → passage |
| Center workspace | active view canvas |
| Right inspector | context-sensitive properties for selected object |
| Bottom console | render jobs, diagnostics, event log, warnings, version notes |

This shell matters because the revised product is not merely an editor. It is an authoring-analysis-rendering environment. The shared shell makes that legible. [filecite: turn1file57] [filecite: turn1file60]

---

##### 4. `$PATTERN_VIEW`

###### 4.1 Purpose

`$PATTERN_VIEW` is the micro-compositional core. It is where the user edits timed phrase-events with tracker-like precision. Rows represent discrete temporal units. Columns represent voice-channels. Cells hold phrase-events and command data. This is the view in which language most explicitly becomes executable score. [filecite: turn1file67]

###### 4.2 Screen model

| Region | Content | Notes |
|---|---|---|
| Pattern header | passage name, row resolution, loop length, swing / subdivision controls | sets local timing context |
| Voice-channel column strip | one column per `$VOICE_CHANNEL` | reorderable, color-coded |
| Phrase-event grid | row-addressed event matrix | central authoring surface |
| Command lanes | per-row command cells adjacent to phrase-event cells | critical for timing and behavior control |
| Mini overview rail | compressed density map of the passage | fast navigation in long patterns |
| Selection inspector | phrase text, entry rule, duration rule, repeat rule, overlap rule, emphasis, spatial rule | right-side contextual editor |
| Bottom phrase editor | expanded text editing for selected event | allows semantic revision without leaving timing context |

###### 4.3 What the user can do here

The user writes or imports phrase-events, assigns them to voice-channels, positions them by row, declares recurrence, and attaches speech commands such as pause, retrigger, cue, overlap, density, breath insertion, or transform behavior. The important point is that these are first-class score operations, not loose annotations. [filecite: turn1file67]

###### 4.4 Primary interactions

| Interaction | Result |
|---|---|
| keyboard entry into a cell | creates or edits a `$PHRASE_EVENT` |
| row drag | retimes event start |
| edge drag | changes local duration behavior |
| command entry | modifies performance execution at exact row position |
| duplicate / interpolate | structural editing across repeated rows |
| channel fold / solo / mute | isolates voice-channels during editing |
| local loop audition | plays a bounded region repeatedly for revision |

###### 4.5 MVP boundary for `$PATTERN_VIEW`

In MVP, this view should be simplified but real. It should support row-based phrase-event editing, basic pause / repeat / emphasis control, channel assignment, and local loop audition. It does not yet need full overlapping polyphony, nested phrase logic, or advanced command grammar. That preserves the narrow proof that users will pay to hear and revise dialogue as performed time. [filecite: turn1file59]

---

##### 5. `$SESSION_VIEW`

###### 5.1 Purpose

`$SESSION_VIEW` is the launch and rehearsal surface. It is where passages are grouped into playable cells for audition, recombination, and exploratory performance. This is the product’s most legible bridge between dramatic revision and live compositional play. [filecite: turn1file58] [filecite: turn1file67]

###### 5.2 Screen model

| Region | Content | Notes |
|---|---|---|
| Session scene strip | vertical stack of launchable rows | each row is a combined launch state across channels |
| Voice-channel lanes | horizontal lanes holding launchable passage states | one lane per channel or grouped ensemble |
| Launch cells | playable passage references | user-surface object; internally still passage / phrase-event references |
| Master launch controls | quantization, trigger mode, stop-all, return-to-anchor | central to rehearsal utility |
| Variant panel | alternate render behaviors per launch state | neutral, heightened, rhythm-forward, diagnostic |
| Monitoring strip | currently active passages, elapsed time, queued launches | makes rehearsal state legible |
| Right inspector | selected launch-state metadata | launch conditions, follow actions, routing, humanization |

###### 5.3 What the user can do here

The user can audition alternate passage combinations, trigger scene states in varying order, rehearse transitions, compare readings, and discover structures that may later be fixed in the arrangement. This is not merely playback. It is exploratory staging logic. [filecite: turn1file55] [filecite: turn1file67]

###### 5.4 Primary interactions

| Interaction | Result |
|---|---|
| launch cell click | triggers selected passage state |
| launch row click | triggers combined state across all active lanes |
| queue next | stages the next state without immediate execution |
| quantize launch | aligns state change to row, beat, or measure |
| capture to arrangement | writes current launch sequence into `$ARRANGEMENT_VIEW` |
| compare modes | hears same material under alternate interpretive renders |
| stop voice-channel | cuts one lane while allowing others to continue |

###### 5.5 MVP boundary for `$SESSION_VIEW`

In MVP, this view should exist as a pragmatic launch grid rather than a full live-performance engine. It needs launchable passages, quantized triggering, basic interpretive mode comparison, and capture-to-arrangement. It does not yet need rule-bound indeterminacy, audience input, or conductor infrastructure. [filecite: turn1file59]

---

##### 6. `$ARRANGEMENT_VIEW`

###### 6.1 Purpose

`$ARRANGEMENT_VIEW` is the macro-form and final-structure surface. It organizes movements, passages, and phrase-event groupings across a linear work timeline. It is where pacing arcs, section boundaries, spatial envelopes, and exportable formal order become explicit. [filecite: turn1file57] [filecite: turn1file67]

###### 6.2 Screen model

| Region | Content | Notes |
|---|---|---|
| Timeline ruler | clock time, beat time, locator markers | switchable display modes |
| Movement lanes | high-level structural blocks | define the work’s major formal zones |
| Voice-channel tracks | stacked horizontal timeline tracks | each track holds scheduled passage / phrase-event material |
| Envelope lanes | density, emphasis, spatialization, pace drift | performance modulation over time |
| Locator strip | named anchors for rehearsal and export | indispensable for navigation |
| Bottom detail editor | selected region, anchor, envelope, or timing edit | fine control without cluttering main timeline |
| Right inspector | selection metadata | timing substrate values, render modes, export flags |

###### 6.3 What the user can do here

The user fixes structure, aligns passages across channels, places locators, shapes pacing over long duration, and prepares renderable output. This is the view in which a fluid exploratory composition becomes a stable work. It is also the place from which rehearsal packs and table-read renders should most naturally be generated. [filecite: turn1file57] [filecite: turn1file60]

###### 6.4 Primary interactions

| Interaction | Result |
|---|---|
| drag passage on timeline | moves scheduled material in formal time |
| trim region | changes section boundary |
| insert locator | creates repeatable navigation anchor |
| draw envelope | modulates intensity, density, spatialization, or pace over time |
| lock utterance anchor | preserves phrase alignment against future retiming |
| consolidate selection | turns exploratory structure into stable passage |
| export render / rehearsal pack | produces artifacts for listening or rehearsal |

###### 6.5 MVP boundary for `$ARRANGEMENT_VIEW`

In MVP, this view should support linear arrangement, locators, basic envelopes, scheduled passages, and exportable table-read rendering. It does not yet need fully elastic warp editing, production-grade automation complexity, or live branching logic. [filecite: turn1file59]

---

##### 7. Cross-view workflow

The three views should form one intelligible workflow rather than three isolated modes.

| Stage | Dominant view | Outcome |
|---|---|---|
| draft as score | `$PATTERN_VIEW` | phrase-events are structured and timed |
| audition variants | `$SESSION_VIEW` | alternate relations and launches are tested |
| formalize work | `$ARRANGEMENT_VIEW` | large-scale order is fixed |
| inspect and revise | back across all three | diagnostics and hearing drive iteration |
| render and export | arrangement-led, pattern-backed | table-read audio, readable script, rehearsal pack |

This sequence preserves the original architecture: authorship, notation, analysis, rehearsal, rendering, execution. The views are merely the concrete interactive manifestation of those layers. [filecite: turn1file57] [filecite: turn1file63]

---

##### 8. Diagnostics placement

The diagnostics layer should not live in only one screen. It must be cross-cutting.

| View | Diagnostic emphasis |
|---|---|
| `$PATTERN_VIEW` | repetition density, dead rows, weak escalation, local pacing friction |
| `$SESSION_VIEW` | launch-state coherence, contrast between variants, unstable transitions |
| `$ARRANGEMENT_VIEW` | overlong sections, flat pacing arcs, weak alternation, structural congestion |

This keeps the `$ANALYSIS_ENGINE` tied to actual compositional work rather than relegating it to a separate critique screen. [filecite: turn1file57] [filecite: turn1file64]

---

##### 9. Revised MVP statement

The revised MVP is no longer just a text pane plus readback transport. It is a three-surface composition environment with one narrow business proof and one deferred architectural horizon.

The MVP proves that a user can take written dramatic language, convert it into structured phrase-events, audition it in playable launch states, arrange it on a formal timeline, and hear the result as performed time. The system still excludes advanced overlap composition, deep live control, and institutional administration, but it now establishes the actual interaction grammar that later differentiates the product. [filecite: turn1file58] [filecite: turn1file59] [filecite: turn1file67]

---

##### 10. Final design rule

`$PATTERN_VIEW` governs **event grammar**.
`$SESSION_VIEW` governs **exploratory relation**.
`$ARRANGEMENT_VIEW` governs **formal order**.

That is the cleanest way to integrate tracker precision and launch-based performance logic without losing the speech-score ontology. [filecite: turn1file67] [filecite: turn1file63]

The next artifact should be a screen-by-screen annotated wireframe package aligned to this spec.

## Response

Message ID: `40734158-b27c-465f-83f1-6d5d85bb29c2`
Created UTC: `2026-03-30T12:13:02.785647Z`
Model: `gpt-5-4-thinking`

Yes. The correct move is **not** a static mockup. The correct move is a **small functional browser prototype** that proves one behavior: a user can take dialogue from page to audible, revisable, shareable performance-time in one tight loop. Your own MVP materials already define that as the first thing to prove. [filecite: turn2file0] [filecite: turn2file2]

#### 1. Define the proof correctly

For this project, the prototype and the proof of concept should be the same artifact.

A silent Figma file would only prove layout. It would not prove the thing that matters here, which is that dialogue becomes a temporal object, can be heard immediately, can be revised against sound, and can then be shared as a review artifact. The clearest product surface is the **audio-dramaturgical studio** layer, not the full theatrical operating system. [filecite: turn2file0] [filecite: turn1file13]

So the first proof should be:

**paste scene → parse speakers → assign voices → play scene → adjust pace/pause → inspect timeline/diagnostics → save version → generate read-only share link.** [filecite: turn2file0] [filecite: turn2file2]

#### 2. Use one canonical demo scene

Use the Philip Glass bakery material as the **seed demonstration work**.

Do not try to prove the whole category with many scenes at once. Prove it with one sample that already contains the transition from ordinary dramatic dialogue into patterned, score-like distribution. That gives you both an accessible entry case and a glimpse of the deeper system. The early product is for hearing and revising dialogue; the later system grows into score-based composition. [filecite: turn1file8] [filecite: turn2file0]

For the proof, I would structure the sample as four `$VOICE_CHANNEL`s: `FIRST_WOMAN`, `SECOND_WOMAN`, `GLASS`, `BAKER`, with stage directions optionally voiced by a neutral narrator or hidden from playback. That stays inside the MVP model cleanly. [filecite: turn1file3] [filecite: turn2file2]

#### 3. Keep the prototype surface very small

The smallest convincing prototype is only **four screens**.

##### Screen 1: New Scene / Import

Paste the script, show the expected `SPEAKER: line` convention, and let the user load the sample instantly. [filecite: turn2file1]

##### Screen 2: Parse Review

Show raw text on one side and parsed speakers/line groupings on the other, with rename and merge controls. This is a trust screen. [filecite: turn2file1]

##### Screen 3: Scene Workspace

This is the actual product: script editor on the left, playback in the center, diagnostics and speaker controls on the right, plus global pace and replay-region controls. The docs are explicit that this screen is the center of gravity. [filecite: turn2file1]

##### Screen 4: Share View

A read-only artifact with the scene title, audio player, text, speaker labels, and optional diagnostics summary. No editing. This is your shareable proof. [filecite: turn2file1] [filecite: turn1file6]

That alone is enough to demonstrate the category.

#### 4. Be ruthless about what is out of scope

For the first proof, do **not** build true overlap composition, conductor tooling, live performance sync, deep collaboration, classroom admin, or full spatial-score editing. Your own spec explicitly defers those. [filecite: turn1file6]

The proof must stay inside the first narrow proposition: people will use a tool that lets them hear dialogue quickly, inspect temporal structure, revise, save versions, and share a performative draft. [filecite: turn2file2]

#### 5. The internal model matters immediately

Even though the prototype surface is small, the data model should **not** be a plain text blob.

You should store a mutable `scene`, immutable `scene_version`s, speaker objects, renders, diagnostics, and share links. That split between editable current state and immutable shareable/renderable state is one of the most important architectural decisions in the system. Without it, version trust and reproducible sharing get weak very quickly. [filecite: turn2file1]

In practice, the POC needs these objects at minimum: `scene`, `speaker`, `scene_version`, `playback_render`, `diagnostic_report`, and `share_link`. [filecite: turn2file2] [filecite: turn2file1]

#### 6. The fastest build shape

Use a thin browser-first stack.

A React or similar stateful front end is appropriate for the workspace. Back it with a simple REST API, PostgreSQL, an async render worker, and object storage for generated audio. That exact stack shape is already recommended in the system package because render jobs should not block the request cycle. [filecite: turn1file14]

#### 7. What the shareable proof should look like

A convincing shareable POC is a **single private URL** that opens to:

the script,
synchronized playback,
speaker labels,
basic timing controls,
one diagnostic summary,
and a stable version label.

That is enough for a dramaturg, playwright, director, or teacher to understand the concept immediately. It also matches the intended MVP share behavior: read-only, audio plus text, review-ready, revocable. [filecite: turn1file6] [filecite: turn2file1]

#### 8. The exact milestone sequence

##### Milestone A

Hard-code one sample scene and one voice assignment profile. Get first playback working.

##### Milestone B

Add parse review, editable speakers, and global pace / pause controls.

##### Milestone C

Add scene versions, one lightweight diagnostic layer, and a speaker timeline.

##### Milestone D

Add read-only share view and a stable share link.

At that point, you already have a real proof of concept. The product has demonstrated the listening-and-revision loop your documents define as the core behavioral thesis. [filecite: turn2file2] [filecite: turn1file7]

#### 9. What comes immediately after

Only after that proof is working should you move into the more visibly original layer: `$PATTERN_VIEW`, `$SESSION_VIEW`, and `$ARRANGEMENT_VIEW` on top of the same temporal dialogue model.

That is the second-phase “wow” move. The first-phase “sell” move is the smaller, sharper workbench. Your own architecture already separates those two layers clearly. [filecite: turn2file0]

The next logical artifact is a **screen-by-screen POC build spec** for those four MVP screens, with the bakery sample pre-modeled as demo content.

Agreed. I treated that as a hard requirement and updated the spec accordingly.

The consequence is structural: this cannot be implemented as “script text plus playback.” It has to be implemented as **ordered timed events** from day one. The UI can stay legible and writer-friendly, but underneath it the scene has to behave like a tracker sequence.

So the POC now implicitly requires this architecture:

Each spoken unit is a bounded event, not just a visual line.

Event order is deterministic.

Selected ranges replay like phrase loops, not vague scrub regions.

Step-through behavior should work event by event.

Pace changes and pause changes must be explicit controls, not fuzzy rendering behavior.

The workspace is now framed as the seed of later `$PATTERN_VIEW`, even if that full view is not yet exposed.

That is the right decision. If tracker-time is essential to you, it should enter at the **timing model**, not get bolted on later at the interface layer. Otherwise you end up rebuilding the core.

**a tracker-compatible temporal data model and interaction spec for the POC workspace**

That artifact would define the event row structure, sequence order rules, loop/range semantics, transport behavior, and how the bakery sample maps into timed event units.

#### Direct answer

The right prototype is a **browser-first coded proof**, not a slide deck and not the full theatrical OS. It should prove one tight loop: paste a scene, parse speakers, hear playback, adjust pace and pauses, inspect timing/diagnostics, save a version, and share a read-only review link. That is the smallest proof that still preserves the real product. [filecite: turn3file0] [filecite: turn3file11]

Because tracker-like time is essential for you, the proof should be built as a **hybrid of tracker precision and Ableton-style launch/arrangement control**. In practice, that means the MVP should visibly include a simplified `$PATTERN_VIEW`, a basic `$SESSION_VIEW`, and a basic `$ARRANGEMENT_VIEW`, alongside voice-channels, clip or scene triggering, global tempo, per-event pause values, locator markers, versioned table-read audio, and a first pass at per-cell speech commands. [filecite: turn3file3] [filecite: turn3file16]

#### What the prototype should actually be

At the product surface, keep it framed as a **listening-first revision environment for performative text**. That is the adoptable wedge. Underneath, keep the deeper ontology intact: speech is stored as structured temporal objects, not inert text, so later expansion into overlap, score logic, and live execution remains possible. [filecite: turn3file10] [filecite: turn3file8]

The prototype should therefore center one main workspace. The documented screen model is already correct: a scene import screen, a parse-review screen, then a three-pane scene workspace with script editor on the left, playback and synchronized focus in the center, and speakers, diagnostics, versions, and share actions on the right. That workspace is the product. [filecite: turn3file12] [filecite: turn3file6]

For the tracker part, rows should represent discrete time units, columns should represent `$VOICE_CHANNEL`s, and each cell should hold a `$PHRASE_EVENT` plus command data such as pause, repeat, overlap, cue, density, or transform. The docs already name this direction explicitly: tracker logic should govern micro-form and event control, while Ableton-like views govern launch, arrangement, automation, and macro navigation. [filecite: turn3file16] [filecite: turn3file3]

#### What the first shareable proof of concept should contain

The shareable artifact should not just be “audio export.” It should be a **read-only review page** for a chosen version: playback player, text, speaker labels, and a compact diagnostics summary. The owner can share it externally, but collaborators do not edit there. That makes it legible as a private development instrument rather than a public publishing surface. [filecite: turn3file9] [filecite: turn3file17]

Architecturally, the critical move is the split between mutable `scene` and immutable `scene_version`. The scene is the working draft. The version is the frozen, renderable, analyzable, shareable artifact. Without that split, your proof of concept will feel flimsy; with it, versions, comparisons, and share links become trustworthy. [filecite: turn3file5] [filecite: turn3file2]

#### What to defer

Do **not** try to prove everything at once. The docs are clear that true simultaneous overlap composition, visual score editing, live conductor tooling, deep collaboration, and broader production infrastructure should stay out of MVP. You need the revision loop first, not the full cathedral. [filecite: turn3file1] [filecite: turn3file4]

That means the first proof should show that someone can get from blank scene to first playback quickly, replay multiple times, revise against hearing, save versions, and generate a real share link. That behavioral loop matters more than spectacle. [filecite: turn3file8]

#### Recommended build order

I would build this in three passes.

First, build a **thin but real coded alpha** around one hard-coded or lightly imported sample. Implement `$PATTERN_VIEW`, `$SESSION_VIEW`, and `$ARRANGEMENT_VIEW` as shallow but functional surfaces, with transport, tempo, locator markers, line highlighting, and read-only share output. This proves the tracker/Ableton fusion visually and temporally before you spend energy on broad ingestion. [filecite: turn3file3] [filecite: turn3file16]

Second, add the **core authoring loop**: script paste/import, speaker parsing, speaker assignment, voice assignment, line and scene playback, pace and pause controls, diagnostics, version save, compare, and share. That is the smallest commercially legible product. [filecite: turn3file7] [filecite: turn3file1]

Third, add the first genuinely tracker-native features: per-cell commands, phrase rows, pattern sequencing, and deterministic replay behavior. That is where the product stops feeling like “script playback” and starts feeling like compositional infrastructure. [filecite: turn3file16] [filecite: turn3file3]

#### Technical shape

The underlying system should be browser-first, with a typed API, a queue-backed render worker, relational storage, and object storage for audio. In your own terms, I would treat the minimum infrastructure as `$APP_WEB`, `$APP_API`, `$APP_WORKER`, `$APP_DB`, `$OBJECT_STORE_URI`, and `$TTS_PROVIDER_URI`. What matters most is not the brand choice but preserving structured temporal dialogue objects, version immutability, and fast render turnaround. [filecite: turn3file2] [filecite: turn3file4]

Latency matters more here than in many normal apps. The docs are right: if playback feels like batch processing, the dramaturgical habit breaks. So the proof should prefer short-scene responsiveness, partial re-rendering, and replay of selected regions over heavyweight “export” thinking. [filecite: turn3file1] [filecite: turn3file6]

#### The acceptance test

The proof of concept is successful when a playwright or dramaturg can create a scene, hear it, inspect temporal structure, revise it, save versions, and share a reviewable artifact **without needing other human performers**. The stronger test is whether they choose it over silent rereading for part of their drafting process. [filecite: turn3file8]

#### Bottom line

So: make the prototype a **shareable browser app with three canonical views**. Let `$PATTERN_VIEW` prove tracker time, let `$SESSION_VIEW` prove modular launch and audition, let `$ARRANGEMENT_VIEW` prove long-form structure, and make the read-only share page the public proof. That is the shortest route from your images to a real, legible artifact. [filecite: turn3file16] [filecite: turn3file17]

I can turn this next into a concrete **screen-by-screen prototype spec for `$PATTERN_VIEW`, `$SESSION_VIEW`, `$ARRANGEMENT_VIEW`, and `$SHARE_VIEW`**.

Would this work in max msp or supercollider or something?

## Response

Message ID: `4ff58680-4503-4d86-92e3-e3e36c1506d8`
Created UTC: `2026-03-30T22:45:23.198426Z`
Model: `gpt-5-4-thinking`

#### Yes — but not all in the same role

It would work in **Max/MSP** and it would work in **SuperCollider**, but they are better for different layers of the system.

Your own spec already implies a split between a browser-first product surface and a deeper temporal kernel. The MVP is supposed to be fast, shareable, versioned, and browser-first, while the deeper engine needs a real `$TIMING_SUBSTRATE`, render flow, and later a `$LIVE_EXECUTION_LAYER`. [filecite: turn4file6] [filecite: turn4file3] [filecite: turn4file19]

So the clean answer is:

**use Max/MSP or SuperCollider as engine/prototyping layers, not as the whole product surface.**

#### Which one fits which job

##### Max/MSP

Max is stronger if your immediate goal is a **performable prototype**: transport, cueing, routing, live triggering, conductor logic, text-event playback, spatialization, and interactive control surfaces. That lines up well with the parts of your system concerned with cue logic, click logic, rehearsal support, and live execution. Your concept explicitly needs tempo, subdivision, cue logic, conductor logic, and algorithmic alignment, which is exactly the sort of thing Max is good at in practice. [filecite: turn4file7] [filecite: turn4file19]

If you want to stand in a room and say, “here is the speech-score grid; here are the voices; here is the trigger matrix; here is the timing,” Max is a very plausible first proof.

##### SuperCollider

SuperCollider is stronger if your immediate goal is the **formal timing engine** itself: deterministic scheduling, recurrence, phase offsets, generative transformation, and text-as-score behavior. Your system definition already centers `$PHRASE_EVENT`, `$TEMPORAL_RELATION`, and `$TIMING_SUBSTRATE`; SuperCollider is very well aligned with that deeper, more compositional layer. [filecite: turn4file16] [filecite: turn4file19]

If what you most want to prove is that speech can be sequenced like tracker data — rows, offsets, repeats, canons, cue chains, elastic timing — SuperCollider is the more rigorous engine core.

#### What each one is bad at

Max/MSP is not the ideal place to build the full commercial wedge of the product: projects, versions, diagnostics, parse review, share links, and the browser-first listening-revision workflow. Your MVP docs are explicit that the application surface should be browser-first, with scenes, versions, playback, diagnostics, and share views as first-class product objects. [filecite: turn4file1] [filecite: turn4file3]

SuperCollider is even less suited to being the whole user-facing product. It is powerful as a timing and synthesis/composition engine, but weak as the main environment for the adoptable product layer whose job is “paste a scene, assign speakers, hear it, revise it, save it, share it.” That workflow is the proof point. [filecite: turn4file2] [filecite: turn4file4]

#### The best architecture is hybrid

The strongest shape is:

`$APP_WEB` = browser editor, versions, diagnostics, share links
`$TIMING_ENGINE` = SuperCollider for row-precise scheduling and recurrence
`$LIVE_ENGINE` = Max/MSP for cueing, routing, triggering, rehearsal, and performance control
`$RENDER_WORKER` = async render pipeline for table-read exports
`$BRIDGE_PROTOCOL` = OSC or WebSocket bridge between layers

That architecture matches your system much better than choosing one environment and forcing it to do everything. It also preserves the rule that the system must not collapse into a generic voice wrapper; it keeps language as structured temporal data while still giving you live-performance power. [filecite: turn4file8] [filecite: turn4file12]

#### What I would do first

If the question is **“What gets me to a convincing proof quickly?”**, I would do this:

Build `$PROTO_01` in **Max/MSP** if the main goal is a room-demo: four voice-channels, tracker-like step grid, phrase triggers, tempo map, repeat commands, conductor transport, and simple TTS or prerecorded speech playback. That proves the theatrical-musical mechanism fast.

Build `$PROTO_02` in **SuperCollider** if the main goal is to validate the deeper engine: a row-based `$PHRASE_EVENT` sequencer with deterministic timing, pattern repetition, phase displacement, and render-to-audio output.

Then build `$APP_WEB` only after the engine behavior feels right. The browser app is where the shareable proof becomes legible to playwrights and dramaturgs, but Max or SuperCollider can prove the engine before that.

#### My recommendation

For your exact concern — **time and sequences proceeding like music trackers** — I would lean like this:

**SuperCollider for the tracker-brain.**
**Max/MSP for the live-performance body.**
**Browser app for the commercial/shareable face.**

That is the cleanest division of labor.

If you want the shortest path, start with **Max/MSP** for a visible, audible prototype. If you want the deepest formal correctness, start with **SuperCollider**. If you want the actual product wedge, neither should be the final front end. The product surface still wants to be browser-first. [filecite: turn4file1] [filecite: turn4file17]

#### Bottom line

Yes. It would work.

But the most correct answer is not **“Max or SuperCollider?”**
It is **“Max for live prototyping, SuperCollider for temporal composition logic, browser for the shareable product.”**

I can sketch a concrete `$PROTO_01` architecture in either **Max/MSP-first** or **SuperCollider-first** form.
